# Microsoft Entra ID | CISO Assistant

For the complete documentation index, see [llms.txt](https://intuitem.gitbook.io/ciso-assistant/llms.txt)
. This page is also available as [Markdown](https://intuitem.gitbook.io/ciso-assistant/features-focus/sso/identity-providers/microsoft-entra-id.md)
.

SAML

OIDC

Go into your **Azure portal home**

1.  Open the sidebar menu and click on **Microsoft Entra ID**
    
    ![](https://intuitem.gitbook.io/ciso-assistant/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F217025809-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FUJGpmCYDFJNsz2CDasSm%252Fuploads%252FcHP2EYPmcTHmLHfWxwwo%252Fentra-sso-step-1.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3D21eedb4e-acd9-40e7-87a1-8d2500f955d3&width=768&dpr=3&quality=100&sign=44a35b06&sv=2)
    
2.  Click on **Add button > Entreprise application**
    
    ![](https://intuitem.gitbook.io/ciso-assistant/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F217025809-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FUJGpmCYDFJNsz2CDasSm%252Fuploads%252FhQSq80CMZRcIyPh3TTiX%252Fentra-sso-step-2.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3D8528f2b1-5c8e-4a28-a465-1ca15b01f641&width=768&dpr=3&quality=100&sign=9b2de74d&sv=2)
    
3.  Click on **Create your own application**
    
    ![](https://intuitem.gitbook.io/ciso-assistant/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F217025809-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FUJGpmCYDFJNsz2CDasSm%252Fuploads%252FsWAqY2buSyov5HUVxOwb%252Fentra-sso-step-3.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3D8962295d-6b85-48dd-8125-02a79525aef0&width=768&dpr=3&quality=100&sign=90af19ff&sv=2)
    
4.  Enter a name and then click **Integrate any other application you don’t find in the gallery (Non-gallery)**
    
    ![](https://intuitem.gitbook.io/ciso-assistant/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F217025809-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FUJGpmCYDFJNsz2CDasSm%252Fuploads%252FtsRDlW8OWeGkZ5A1Yugg%252Fentra-sso-step-4.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3D2fa3b826-97f5-45f1-b143-a4f1db02b673&width=768&dpr=3&quality=100&sign=a86d5b1f&sv=2)
    
5.  Click on **Single sign-on** from the sidebar menu or on **Set up single sign on** bellow Getting Started and choose **SAML**
    
    ![](https://intuitem.gitbook.io/ciso-assistant/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F217025809-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FUJGpmCYDFJNsz2CDasSm%252Fuploads%252FTqOEyhtgK3FpNb3XI3pY%252Fentra-sso-step-5-1.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3Dfb135a7c-839b-41a1-8a38-0829fdb2107f&width=768&dpr=3&quality=100&sign=1719fdf2&sv=2)
    
    ![](https://intuitem.gitbook.io/ciso-assistant/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F217025809-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FUJGpmCYDFJNsz2CDasSm%252Fuploads%252F3FSPwKykdceU9OxGjBqG%252Fentra-sso-step-5-2.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3D18b5e840-30b8-4ea6-a6ca-2b79d9a39f96&width=768&dpr=3&quality=100&sign=eea4007c&sv=2)
    
6.  In the first box **Basic SAML Configuration**, specify the **Entity ID**, it has to be the same than **SP Entity ID** in CISO Assistant (see next screenshot)
    
7.  Add the **Reply URL**: `<base_url>/api/accounts/saml/0/acs/` (for example with localhost: `https://localhost:8443/api/accounts/saml/0/acs/`)
    
    ![](https://intuitem.gitbook.io/ciso-assistant/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F217025809-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FUJGpmCYDFJNsz2CDasSm%252Fuploads%252FZjUwAWHhahnddVce11eT%252Fentra-sso-step-6-7.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3D01614726-84bc-4192-a1ae-8ed46f331979&width=768&dpr=3&quality=100&sign=501024bd&sv=2)
    
8.  In the third box **SAML Certificates**, copy the **App Federation Metadata Url** as it is the **Metadata URL** in CISO Assistant (see next screenshot)
    
9.  In the fourth box **Set up <App\_name>**, copy the **Microsoft Entra Identifier** as it is the **IdP Entity ID** in CISO Assistant
    
    ![](https://intuitem.gitbook.io/ciso-assistant/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F217025809-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FUJGpmCYDFJNsz2CDasSm%252Fuploads%252FTexEzK031txIw2uUm1Ga%252Fentra-sso-step-8-9.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3Db1572516-ce09-41dc-98e9-41d15863e18e&width=768&dpr=3&quality=100&sign=7864d459&sv=2)
    
10.  Make sure you use the same Identifier (Entity ID) that you've set earlier and appear on block 1, on CISO Assistant SP Entity ID: ![](https://intuitem.gitbook.io/ciso-assistant/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F217025809-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FUJGpmCYDFJNsz2CDasSm%252Fuploads%252FGZHS1FzeUDuurXdoEN6i%252Fimage.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3D429eee78-4f3d-4737-ac2d-2d87441ec41f&width=300&dpr=3&quality=100&sign=5d2f81ff&sv=2)
    
11.  Click on **Users and groups** in the sidebar menu, and **Add user/group** to give them access to CISO Assistant with SSO. The matching key will be the email and you'll be able to grant their permissions on the applications.
    
    ![](https://intuitem.gitbook.io/ciso-assistant/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F217025809-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FUJGpmCYDFJNsz2CDasSm%252Fuploads%252FpLl77BIJIhizW9qZLE8J%252Fentra-sso-step-10.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3D98fcdb84-0c24-4870-be3a-cf30c40a0e0f&width=768&dpr=3&quality=100&sign=c8957562&sv=2)
    
12.  You can now [configure CISO Assistant](https://intuitem.gitbook.io/ciso-assistant/features-focus/sso#configure-ciso-assistant-with-saml)
     with the **3 parameters** you've retrieved.

Go to your Microsoft Azure Portal

6\. Enter the callback URL of your instance

The callback URL is: `<ciso_assistant_url>/api/accounts/oidc/openid_connect/login/callback/` for

for instance, for localhost: `http://localhost:8000/api/accounts/oidc/openid_connect/login/callback/`

[](https://intuitem.gitbook.io/ciso-assistant/features-focus/sso/identity-providers/microsoft-entra-id#id-8.-copy-the-application-client-id)

8\. Copy the Application Client ID

![](https://intuitem.gitbook.io/ciso-assistant/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2Fstatic.guidde.com%2Fv0%2Fqg%252FIEuhINveF1g6sYuIJ0IpcFfUJDz2%252Frk5UfQgUTG1bXn6gWdkGLo%252Fj4HxbA933shMF4YLiTQpKN_doc.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3D7d23b6bd-824f-4e8e-ab24-c8d19cb76ef7&width=768&dpr=3&quality=100&sign=5cae5cce&sv=2)

Copy the Application Client ID

#### 

[](https://intuitem.gitbook.io/ciso-assistant/features-focus/sso/identity-providers/microsoft-entra-id#id-9.-past-it-into-the-client-id-field)

9\. Past it into the Client ID field

![](https://intuitem.gitbook.io/ciso-assistant/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2Fstatic.guidde.com%2Fv0%2Fqg%252FIEuhINveF1g6sYuIJ0IpcFfUJDz2%252Frk5UfQgUTG1bXn6gWdkGLo%252FmfJwdmC6XW98TwQtBi1tDE_doc.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3Df785e518-1d5b-4a5a-b329-56a767012b6e&width=768&dpr=3&quality=100&sign=a05e3057&sv=2)

Past it into the Client ID field

#### 

[](https://intuitem.gitbook.io/ciso-assistant/features-focus/sso/identity-providers/microsoft-entra-id#id-10.-open-certificates-and-secrets)

10\. Open Certificates & Secrets

![](https://intuitem.gitbook.io/ciso-assistant/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2Fstatic.guidde.com%2Fv0%2Fqg%252FIEuhINveF1g6sYuIJ0IpcFfUJDz2%252Frk5UfQgUTG1bXn6gWdkGLo%252FtSEeuLJhWcgbv2kCSDFa5W_doc.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3Dc4cb2f78-ab54-4647-a3eb-7c7abe4231b9&width=768&dpr=3&quality=100&sign=d40fedfa&sv=2)

Open Certificates & Secrets

#### 

[](https://intuitem.gitbook.io/ciso-assistant/features-focus/sso/identity-providers/microsoft-entra-id#id-11.-create-a-new-client-secret)

11\. Create a New Client Secret

![](https://intuitem.gitbook.io/ciso-assistant/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2Fstatic.guidde.com%2Fv0%2Fqg%252FIEuhINveF1g6sYuIJ0IpcFfUJDz2%252Frk5UfQgUTG1bXn6gWdkGLo%252F2bUjbaZCmeRE4tAm5wXYmV_doc.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3Db04156e4-b8d4-45ee-846d-81364ffce675&width=768&dpr=3&quality=100&sign=799d41e8&sv=2)

![](https://intuitem.gitbook.io/ciso-assistant/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2Fstatic.guidde.com%2Fv0%2Fqg%252FIEuhINveF1g6sYuIJ0IpcFfUJDz2%252Frk5UfQgUTG1bXn6gWdkGLo%252FquPjbc42FSLh4gdRxQtNbJ_doc.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3D91060f91-e8ca-47fa-9204-7bdc5445ac29&width=768&dpr=3&quality=100&sign=1c73cac9&sv=2)

[](https://intuitem.gitbook.io/ciso-assistant/features-focus/sso/identity-providers/microsoft-entra-id#id-13.-copy-the-fresh-client-secret-value)

13\. Copy the fresh Client Secret Value

![](https://intuitem.gitbook.io/ciso-assistant/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2Fstatic.guidde.com%2Fv0%2Fqg%252FIEuhINveF1g6sYuIJ0IpcFfUJDz2%252Frk5UfQgUTG1bXn6gWdkGLo%252FfhUvXygLkKLWcU2FRbUWCm_doc.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3D19ce3280-9d37-4066-940d-a8056e6c292f&width=768&dpr=3&quality=100&sign=c124d934&sv=2)

[](https://intuitem.gitbook.io/ciso-assistant/features-focus/sso/identity-providers/microsoft-entra-id#id-14.-past-it-into-the-secret-field)

![](https://intuitem.gitbook.io/ciso-assistant/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2Fstatic.guidde.com%2Fv0%2Fqg%252FIEuhINveF1g6sYuIJ0IpcFfUJDz2%252Frk5UfQgUTG1bXn6gWdkGLo%252FdeXjQnv7rSz5g9VfNd6iqJ_doc.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3D72bbf1c7-548e-4acc-abf9-07981f7cdeb5&width=768&dpr=3&quality=100&sign=47321fcd&sv=2)

[](https://intuitem.gitbook.io/ciso-assistant/features-focus/sso/identity-providers/microsoft-entra-id#id-15.-go-back-to-your-app-overview)

![](https://intuitem.gitbook.io/ciso-assistant/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2Fstatic.guidde.com%2Fv0%2Fqg%252FIEuhINveF1g6sYuIJ0IpcFfUJDz2%252Frk5UfQgUTG1bXn6gWdkGLo%252Fk4VkipPBEeDSWX95eva89a_doc.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3D959cd638-397a-465f-8502-1d8a0a8369d9&width=768&dpr=3&quality=100&sign=a331f3d2&sv=2)

You have successfully configured OpenID Connect (OIDC) integration with EntraID.

Adding a user in your Entra application doesn't automatically create the user on CISO Assistant

# Keycloak | CISO Assistant

For the complete documentation index, see [llms.txt](https://intuitem.gitbook.io/ciso-assistant/llms.txt)
. This page is also available as [Markdown](https://intuitem.gitbook.io/ciso-assistant/features-focus/sso/identity-providers/keycloak.md)
.

If Keycloak and CISO Assistant are both deployed locally with docker, you'll need to make sure that both containers can communicate together. You can do this with a [bridge network](https://docs.docker.com/engine/network/drivers/bridge/)
.

SAML

OpenID Connect (OIDC)

Go into your **Keycloak admin console**

1.  Open the sidebar menu > **Clients** and **Create client**
    
    ![](https://intuitem.gitbook.io/ciso-assistant/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F217025809-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FUJGpmCYDFJNsz2CDasSm%252Fuploads%252FaJPj1KcrShXp5yTWeh8e%252FScreenshot%25202024-08-20%252009.40.06.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3D2d0cfafc-d252-49ee-9fa1-fcec49bbdffe&width=768&dpr=3&quality=100&sign=47a5adb4&sv=2)
    
2.  Choose **SAML** client type and name it **ciso-assistant** or with your custom **SP Entity ID**
    
    ![](https://intuitem.gitbook.io/ciso-assistant/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F217025809-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FUJGpmCYDFJNsz2CDasSm%252Fuploads%252F5Hf1gVGOtPEyck8GHbU1%252FScreenshot%25202024-08-20%252009.41.23.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3Dab774765-3be4-4db1-a810-487aebe20ba0&width=768&dpr=3&quality=100&sign=1236dcd0&sv=2)
    
3.  Fill the **Home URL** with your `<base_url>` and **Valid redirect URIs** with `<backend_url/*>`
    
    ![](https://intuitem.gitbook.io/ciso-assistant/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F217025809-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FUJGpmCYDFJNsz2CDasSm%252Fuploads%252FO4vxs3sOMYko8culRz5X%252FScreenshot%25202024-08-20%252009.53.57.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3Da090f23d-088d-4637-80d8-6a3e9f17c96c&width=768&dpr=3&quality=100&sign=3b63f527&sv=2)
    
    If you have some problems to configure these urls you can ask for help on [Discord](https://discord.gg/8C4X7ndQQ4)
     or by emailing us
    
4.  Go into **Keys** and disable **Signing keys config**
    
    ![](https://intuitem.gitbook.io/ciso-assistant/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F217025809-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FUJGpmCYDFJNsz2CDasSm%252Fuploads%252FAJfiCmAUgBeEhRiVjoC6%252FScreenshot%25202024-08-20%252009.57.51.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3Decdb88f7-3ec9-43d2-892f-7c474070c521&width=768&dpr=3&quality=100&sign=f1c37d39&sv=2)
    
5.  Go into **Advanced** and fill **ACS field** with `<backend_url/api/accounts/saml/0/acs/>` (on a cloud instance it is simply `<base_url/api/accounts/saml/0/acs/>`)
    
    ![](https://intuitem.gitbook.io/ciso-assistant/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F217025809-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FUJGpmCYDFJNsz2CDasSm%252Fuploads%252FCIO2BCCmmk6OBwHS8yVS%252FScreenshot%25202024-08-20%252010.01.40.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3D4c4ee706-9606-4e3d-a430-4e867703f798&width=768&dpr=3&quality=100&sign=526ad334&sv=2)
    
6.  Go to **Client scopes** and click on **ciso-assistant-dedicated**
    
    ![](https://intuitem.gitbook.io/ciso-assistant/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F217025809-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FUJGpmCYDFJNsz2CDasSm%252Fuploads%252Fenr92GNZzW2QulLkA4Kj%252FScreenshot%25202024-08-20%252010.04.23.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3D3953a1c4-27ff-4d93-bd78-cbce0acbae9a&width=768&dpr=3&quality=100&sign=4be3b455&sv=2)
    
7.  **Add a predefined mapper** and check all **X500** ones
    
    ![](https://intuitem.gitbook.io/ciso-assistant/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F217025809-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FUJGpmCYDFJNsz2CDasSm%252Fuploads%252FHU2LLdo9rimJaKaGzbAx%252FScreenshot%25202024-08-20%252010.07.22.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3D571e09fe-8a75-428a-ae13-84b048585048&width=768&dpr=3&quality=100&sign=f1248cee&sv=2)
    
8.  Click on **X500 surname** and replace **SAML Attribute name** with `http://schemas.xmlsoap.org/ws/2005/05/identity/claims/surname`
    
    ![](https://intuitem.gitbook.io/ciso-assistant/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F217025809-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FUJGpmCYDFJNsz2CDasSm%252Fuploads%252FRTDrINEyXJ5eFNBMvIvH%252FScreenshot%25202024-08-20%252011.00.15.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3D5ae173dc-1749-4cc9-8538-fdc7c6b34596&width=768&dpr=3&quality=100&sign=4eb2d260&sv=2)
    
9.  Click on **X500 givenName** and replace **SAML Attribute name** with `http://schemas.xmlsoap.org/ws/2005/05/identity/claims/givenname`
    
    ![](https://intuitem.gitbook.io/ciso-assistant/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F217025809-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FUJGpmCYDFJNsz2CDasSm%252Fuploads%252FjUieb0xrY7JpMqHeMCC4%252FScreenshot%25202024-08-20%252011.02.11.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3D574de6d5-0366-47f1-bf61-318b93c1123c&width=768&dpr=3&quality=100&sign=77c3ad64&sv=2)
    
10.  Go into **Realm settings > General**, you will find the **Metadata URL**
    
    ![](https://intuitem.gitbook.io/ciso-assistant/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F217025809-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FUJGpmCYDFJNsz2CDasSm%252Fuploads%252FpH8A2Y6OYSqpbMksDcoz%252FScreenshot%25202024-08-20%252011.14.57.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3D0af50f3b-0201-475d-9e86-c1d7f73bdee4&width=768&dpr=3&quality=100&sign=3f9fdfb3&sv=2)
    
11.  You'll find inside the **Metadata URL** the **Entity ID**
    
    ![](https://intuitem.gitbook.io/ciso-assistant/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F217025809-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FUJGpmCYDFJNsz2CDasSm%252Fuploads%252FwD3kWJ5AzZn1NrMU8PJQ%252FScreenshot%25202024-08-20%252011.15.46.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3Dfe5aae0d-b56a-45d9-ba0b-f4b83a8ad4b3&width=768&dpr=3&quality=100&sign=288ecf48&sv=2)
    

Go into your **Keycloak admin console**

1.  Open the sidebar menu > **Clients** and **Create client**
    
    ![](https://intuitem.gitbook.io/ciso-assistant/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F217025809-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FUJGpmCYDFJNsz2CDasSm%252Fuploads%252FaJPj1KcrShXp5yTWeh8e%252FScreenshot%25202024-08-20%252009.40.06.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3D2d0cfafc-d252-49ee-9fa1-fcec49bbdffe&width=768&dpr=3&quality=100&sign=47a5adb4&sv=2)
    
2.  Choose **OpenID Connect** client type and give it a **Client ID**, then click **Next**![](https://intuitem.gitbook.io/ciso-assistant/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F217025809-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FUJGpmCYDFJNsz2CDasSm%252Fuploads%252FUKXk8pZyDbTHGs1HQGTT%252Fimage.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3Dfba0e5d6-e797-4558-893d-b011afc44761&width=300&dpr=3&quality=100&sign=d321cc01&sv=2)
    
3.  Enable **Client authentication**, make sure **Standard flow** is selected, then click **Next**![](https://intuitem.gitbook.io/ciso-assistant/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F217025809-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FUJGpmCYDFJNsz2CDasSm%252Fuploads%252FfGHfvoYnfrPLzVsZtRzB%252Fimage.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3D9175318a-a99a-48b8-b596-c66060c466a8&width=300&dpr=3&quality=100&sign=27202985&sv=2)
    
4.  Enter your deployment's **Root URL**. It is the URL of your frontend.
    
    1.  Set it to `<frontend_url>`
        
    2.  For cloud deployments, you must set it to `<base_url>`
        
    
5.  Set the **Home URL** to `**/**`
    
6.  Enter your **Valid redirect URIs**
    
    1.  Set it to `<backend_url>/api/accounts/oidc/openid_connect/login/callback/`
        
    2.  For cloud deployments, you must set it to `<base_url>/api/accounts/oidc/openid_connect/login/callback/`
        
        ![](https://intuitem.gitbook.io/ciso-assistant/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F217025809-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FUJGpmCYDFJNsz2CDasSm%252Fuploads%252FfrABqHZsyoKLHP8i4PGn%252Fimage.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3D52409298-910b-4813-8a12-423f5f37ab39&width=768&dpr=3&quality=100&sign=b40338bd&sv=2)
        
    
7.  Once your client is created, you can find its **Client secret** under the **Credentials** tab. You can copy it from there
    
    ![](https://intuitem.gitbook.io/ciso-assistant/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F217025809-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FUJGpmCYDFJNsz2CDasSm%252Fuploads%252FDqzKFd9yZVXtyaziU0FC%252Fimage.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3Daf8d8b67-b6be-4b0c-b9e9-924f76bf20fe&width=768&dpr=3&quality=100&sign=a124b5f4&sv=2)
    
8.  Go into **Realm settings > General** to find the **OpenID Endpoint Configuration**, which you will have to paste into CISO Assistant's **Server URL** SSO parameter
    
    ![](https://intuitem.gitbook.io/ciso-assistant/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F217025809-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FUJGpmCYDFJNsz2CDasSm%252Fuploads%252FbaqN3UFFwtdkHLSvwah1%252Fimage.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3Db91050f9-3b62-4b56-8ffe-22bada4229b4&width=768&dpr=3&quality=100&sign=7b3f9f87&sv=2)
    

Adding a user in your application doesn't automatically create the user on CISO Assistant

You can now [configure CISO Assistant](https://intuitem.gitbook.io/ciso-assistant/features-highlights/sso#configure-ciso-assistant-with-saml)
 with the **parameters** you've retrieved.

[PreviousGoogle Workspace](https://intuitem.gitbook.io/ciso-assistant/features-focus/sso/identity-providers/google-workplace)
[NextSetting up Multi-Factor Authentication (MFA)](https://intuitem.gitbook.io/ciso-assistant/features-focus/setting-up-multi-factor-authentication-mfa)

Last updated 11 months ago

# Add and manage users | CISO Assistant

For the complete documentation index, see [llms.txt](https://intuitem.gitbook.io/ciso-assistant/llms.txt)
. This page is also available as [Markdown](https://intuitem.gitbook.io/ciso-assistant/model/organization/add-and-manage-users.md)
.

Under Organization, click on Users and then Add user:

![](https://intuitem.gitbook.io/ciso-assistant/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F217025809-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FUJGpmCYDFJNsz2CDasSm%252Fuploads%252FwRT0JDJD2slzBKZ0yuhH%252Fimage.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3D224a76d2-b596-4c7e-b876-b039f0f3eb6b&width=768&dpr=3&quality=100&sign=718216e0&sv=2)

Set up the email of the new user:

![](https://intuitem.gitbook.io/ciso-assistant/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F217025809-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FUJGpmCYDFJNsz2CDasSm%252Fuploads%252FGWxXojAJj5TtdSvmyDyA%252Fimage.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3Dcb6f481b-eedf-4c04-b8db-15ca47d0ee41&width=768&dpr=3&quality=100&sign=6caa4cf8&sv=2)

Once created, a new user doesn't have any permissions by default. Click edit and update the user groups:

![](https://intuitem.gitbook.io/ciso-assistant/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F217025809-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FUJGpmCYDFJNsz2CDasSm%252Fuploads%252FE2eJLu8EJL8Nk77wAIaI%252Fimage.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3D66557324-bb61-4588-9374-92a4eb1b26e7&width=768&dpr=3&quality=100&sign=1f2fedbe&sv=2)

If you are working on a single domain, or working on solo, you might just set \`Global - Administrator\`

![](https://intuitem.gitbook.io/ciso-assistant/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F217025809-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FUJGpmCYDFJNsz2CDasSm%252Fuploads%252FDBSMNGRQVYJmJsgNfAQp%252Fimage.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3Df529140e-db4a-4300-92d6-7d47d60df556&width=768&dpr=3&quality=100&sign=4b1fd2a0&sv=2)

When the user are added, and if the mailer is set, he/she will receive an email to set up the password. If not, you can set a temporary password as illustrated above.

# Organization | CISO Assistant

For the complete documentation index, see [llms.txt](https://intuitem.gitbook.io/ciso-assistant/llms.txt)
. This page is also available as [Markdown](https://intuitem.gitbook.io/ciso-assistant/model/organization.md)
.

[](https://intuitem.gitbook.io/ciso-assistant/model/organization#a-folder-organization)

A folder organization


------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

For Access Control purpose, CISO Assistant data is organized in a tree of folders. Starting from a root folder called Global, it divide into sub-folders called domains. The organization of the tree is not hard-coded, it is entirely determined by configuration. Any object in CISO Assistant is attached to a folder (including folders), either directly or indirectly through a parent object that is attached to a folder.

![folder organization](https://intuitem.gitbook.io/ciso-assistant/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F217025809-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FUJGpmCYDFJNsz2CDasSm%252Fuploads%252F5dNMldUgB2CNUMXWDXLh%252FScreenshot%2520from%25202024-03-12%252013-08-27.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3D27dfdb9f-2e44-45b7-a3c6-3fc262f6373d&width=768&dpr=3&quality=100&sign=fefac10d&sv=2)

Organization example

### 

[](https://intuitem.gitbook.io/ciso-assistant/model/organization#so-what-is-a-domain)

So, what is a domain?

A domain permits to organize your work depending on your use of CISO Assistant. For example, inside a company, you can create a domain for each department for which you need to carry out a variety of perimeters, or if you have different customers, you may as well have a domain for each one in order **to delimit your work area**.

#### 

[](https://intuitem.gitbook.io/ciso-assistant/model/organization#utility)

Utility

A domain is the first thing you create on CISO Assistant. It will **bring together** all objects you need to complete your different perimeters. Every **role/permission** a user has on a domain **are applicable to all objects/actions** across the domain. It's all about organization, the only technical aspect is access control, and this is achieved by adding the user to the relevant user group.

#### 

[](https://intuitem.gitbook.io/ciso-assistant/model/organization#role-assignment)

Role assignment

In the first/open source version of CISO Assistant, custom role assignment is not available. So, when you create a domain, user groups concerning this domain are automatically created for each built-in role. All you need to do, is to assign your users to their user groups. To learn more about this, jump to [User Groups](https://intuitem.gitbook.io/ciso-assistant/model/organization/user-groups)
.

[](https://intuitem.gitbook.io/ciso-assistant/model/organization#perimeters)

Perimeters


--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Perimeters are fundamental context objects defined by the entity using CISO Assistant. They are grouped in domains. They will contain all your risk and compliance assessments. Apart from being able to group your various evaluations across the different domains.

There are two specific fields, internal reference and status. Here are the various status options:

*   \-- (None)
    
*   Design
    
*   Development
    
*   Production
    
*   End of life
    
*   Dropped
    

The purpose of a perimeter is at first, it's organizational aspect to solve a problem. But it also makes it possible to improve analytics by breaking them down according to the different assessments, whether for risk or compliance, so as to make your project management more precise and reduce noise.

[](https://intuitem.gitbook.io/ciso-assistant/model/organization#user-groups)

User Groups


----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

User groups go hand in hand with domains. they associate permissions with users and define their scope, by being attached to a domain. They follow a simple and consistent RBAC model from a role containing permissions and a domain determining the perimeter. Go to the [User Groups](https://intuitem.gitbook.io/ciso-assistant/model/organization/user-groups)
 page for more details.

[PreviousAssignments / respondent mode](https://intuitem.gitbook.io/ciso-assistant/features-focus/assignments-respondent-mode)
[NextAdd and manage users](https://intuitem.gitbook.io/ciso-assistant/model/organization/add-and-manage-users)

Last updated 5 months ago

Was this helpful?

*   [A folder organization](https://intuitem.gitbook.io/ciso-assistant/model/organization#a-folder-organization)
    
*   [So, what is a domain?](https://intuitem.gitbook.io/ciso-assistant/model/organization#so-what-is-a-domain)
    
*   [Perimeters](https://intuitem.gitbook.io/ciso-assistant/model/organization#perimeters)
    
*   [User Groups](https://intuitem.gitbook.io/ciso-assistant/model/organization#user-groups)
    

Was this helpful?

# User Groups | CISO Assistant

For the complete documentation index, see [llms.txt](https://intuitem.gitbook.io/ciso-assistant/llms.txt)
. This page is also available as [Markdown](https://intuitem.gitbook.io/ciso-assistant/model/organization/user-groups.md)
.

For now, it is not possible to create custom role assignments so you need to use built-in user groups. They are linking a domain with a role which contains precise permissions, that will be given to users in this group.

### 

[](https://intuitem.gitbook.io/ciso-assistant/model/organization/user-groups#roles)

Roles

Let's give some details on the 5 built-in roles:

Role

Permissions

Administrator

full access (except approval), and specifically management of domains, users and users rights

Domain manager

full access to selected domains (except approval), in particular managing rights for these domains. Read access to global objects

Analyst

read-write access to selected perimeters/domains. Read access to global and domain objects

Reader

read access to selected perimeters/domains

Approver

like reader, but with additional capability to approve risk acceptances

Respondent

see [Assignments / respondent mode](https://intuitem.gitbook.io/ciso-assistant/features-focus/assignments-respondent-mode)
 for more details

Django superuser is given administrator rights automatically on startup.

### 

[](https://intuitem.gitbook.io/ciso-assistant/model/organization/user-groups#global-user-groups)

Global user groups

Once your instance is created, four user groups are already present:

*   Global - Administrator
    
*   Global - Analyst
    
*   Global - Reader
    
*   Global - Approver
    
*   Global - Respondend
    

They give corresponding permissions on Global scope so on every object of your instance.

### 

[](https://intuitem.gitbook.io/ciso-assistant/model/organization/user-groups#domain-user-groups)

Domain user groups

They are created for each domain you add. For example, if you create a domain _R&D_, there will be:

*   R&D - Domain Manager
    
*   R&D - Analyst
    
*   R&D - Reader
    
*   R&D - Approver
    
*   R&D - Respondent
    

They give corresponding permissions on the domain scope so on every object inside _R&D_.

[PreviousAdd and manage users](https://intuitem.gitbook.io/ciso-assistant/model/organization/add-and-manage-users)
[NextCustom roles](https://intuitem.gitbook.io/ciso-assistant/model/organization/custom-roles)

Last updated 4 months ago

Was this helpful?

*   [Roles](https://intuitem.gitbook.io/ciso-assistant/model/organization/user-groups#roles)
    
*   [Global user groups](https://intuitem.gitbook.io/ciso-assistant/model/organization/user-groups#global-user-groups)
    
*   [Domain user groups](https://intuitem.gitbook.io/ciso-assistant/model/organization/user-groups#domain-user-groups)
    

Was this helpful?

# Risk | CISO Assistant

For the complete documentation index, see [llms.txt](https://intuitem.gitbook.io/ciso-assistant/llms.txt)
. This page is also available as [Markdown](https://intuitem.gitbook.io/ciso-assistant/model/risk.md)
.

![](https://intuitem.gitbook.io/ciso-assistant/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F217025809-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FUJGpmCYDFJNsz2CDasSm%252Fuploads%252FEHcKTunnZHDfZIsqv4eh%252Fiso27005.svg%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3D16ed19b2-13c7-4c24-a554-8369b8ede810&width=768&dpr=3&quality=100&sign=7d68ac37&sv=2)

ISO 27005 risk management workflow

[](https://intuitem.gitbook.io/ciso-assistant/model/risk#risk-assessment)

Risk assessment


----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

You can create risk assessments in your perimeters. A risk assessment encompasses:

*   risk identification, when you define your risk scenarios
    
*   risk analysis, when you assess the probability, impact and strength of knowledge for each scenario
    
*   risk evaluation, which is done automatically based on the selected risk matrix
    

In CISO Assistant, risk treatment is combined with risk assessment.

[](https://intuitem.gitbook.io/ciso-assistant/model/risk#risk-scenario)

Risk scenario


------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

The scenarios can be defined directly from the risk assessment view or separately via this view.

[](https://intuitem.gitbook.io/ciso-assistant/model/risk#risk-acceptance)

Risk acceptance


----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Risk acceptance is when an organization or individual decides to tolerate a certain level of risk without taking further action to reduce it. This view allows to manage a workflow to get formal approval of risk acceptances by the management. The approver of a risk acceptance must have a user account with approver role. To find out more about risk acceptance, you can have a look to the [ENISA risk management process](https://www.enisa.europa.eu/topics/risk-management/current-risk/risk-management-inventory/rm-process/risk-acceptance)
.

[PreviousGovernance](https://intuitem.gitbook.io/ciso-assistant/model/governance)
[NextCompliance](https://intuitem.gitbook.io/ciso-assistant/model/compliance)

Last updated 1 year ago

Was this helpful?

*   [Risk assessment](https://intuitem.gitbook.io/ciso-assistant/model/risk#risk-assessment)
    
*   [Risk scenario](https://intuitem.gitbook.io/ciso-assistant/model/risk#risk-scenario)
    
*   [Risk acceptance](https://intuitem.gitbook.io/ciso-assistant/model/risk#risk-acceptance)

# Prerequisites | CISO Assistant

For the complete documentation index, see [llms.txt](https://intuitem.gitbook.io/ciso-assistant/llms.txt)
. This page is also available as [Markdown](https://intuitem.gitbook.io/ciso-assistant/deployment/prerequisites.md)
.

### 

[](https://intuitem.gitbook.io/ciso-assistant/deployment/prerequisites#prerequisites-to-install-ciso-assistant-on-premises)

Prerequisites to Install CISO Assistant On-Premises

1.  **Hardware Requirements:**
    
    1.  CPU: 4 cores
        
    2.  RAM: Minimum 8 GB
        
    3.  Storage: Minimum 10 GB (consider more for evidences)
        
    

You can start with lower specs of course for testing.

1.  **Software Requirements:**
    
    1.  Ubuntu/Debian, CentOS, RHEL: LTS versions recommended when applicable\*
        
    2.  Docker 27 or up, with Docker compose, **or** Kubernetes Cluster 1.31 or up
        
    3.  Postgres 16 or up if you are choosing this variant
        
    4.  Any SMTP compatible Mailer
        
    

\*most Linux distributions supporting Docker should be compatible but have not been tested. Some distributions are not using the official repositories so make sure to follow the instructions from docker page.

[PreviousDomain export/import](https://intuitem.gitbook.io/ciso-assistant/model/domain-export-import)
[NextLocal](https://intuitem.gitbook.io/ciso-assistant/deployment/local)

# Compliance | CISO Assistant

For the complete documentation index, see [llms.txt](https://intuitem.gitbook.io/ciso-assistant/llms.txt)
. This page is also available as [Markdown](https://intuitem.gitbook.io/ciso-assistant/model/compliance.md)
.

[](https://intuitem.gitbook.io/ciso-assistant/model/compliance#framework)

Framework


----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

The fundamental object of CISO Assistant for compliance is the framework. It corresponds to a given **standard**, e.g. ISO27001:2022. They can be imported from the library. If you don't find a framework which fits your needs, no worries, you can build your own framework and add it to CISO Assistant!

[](https://intuitem.gitbook.io/ciso-assistant/model/compliance#audit)

Audit


--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

This allows you to **assess your compliance** with the **chosen framework** through different statuses for each requirement that requires one of the following:

*   To do
    
*   In progress
    
*   Non compliant
    
*   Partially compliant
    
*   Compliant
    
*   Not applicable
    

Evaluate a requirement inside a compliance assessment is called **requirement assessment**

[](https://intuitem.gitbook.io/ciso-assistant/model/compliance#evidence)

Evidence


--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Evidence allows you to use a description, link or file to justify the status of a compliance requirement or to prove that a control has been applied. They can therefore be associated with different [applied controls](https://app.gitbook.com/o/HbfwRhJ3GSwl5w6MOhZw/s/UJGpmCYDFJNsz2CDasSm/~/changes/3/glossary/context#applied-control)
 or requirement assessments.

[PreviousRisk](https://intuitem.gitbook.io/ciso-assistant/model/risk)
[NextManage extended result](https://intuitem.gitbook.io/ciso-assistant/model/compliance/manage-extended-result)

*   [Audit](https://intuitem.gitbook.io/ciso-assistant/model/compliance#audit)

# Local | CISO Assistant

For the complete documentation index, see [llms.txt](https://intuitem.gitbook.io/ciso-assistant/llms.txt)
. This page is also available as [Markdown](https://intuitem.gitbook.io/ciso-assistant/deployment/local.md)
.

The recommended pattern for local deployment is to use **Docker Compose**. Check the Readme file on the CISO Assistant repo for the latest instructions.

The compose file will manage three containers and set the required variables:

*   Front
    
*   Back
    
*   Caddy (proxy)
    

*   Make sure to have a recent version of Docker installed
    
    *   On a Linux distro with a server flavor, make sure to remove older versions and install the latest one using the proper Docker repos to avoid twisted setups. Check out the instructions at [https://docs.docker.com/engine/install/ubuntu/](https://docs.docker.com/engine/install/ubuntu/)
        
    
*   On Windows, Docker Desktop+WSL is recommended
    
*   On MacOS, Docker Desktop covers the requirements
    

### 

[](https://intuitem.gitbook.io/ciso-assistant/deployment/local#using-prebuilt-images)

Using prebuilt images

Run:

Copy

    ./docker-compose.sh

It will clean up previous images and get the latest stable release.

Once the images are downloaded and migration triggered, you should see a prompt asking you to set the first superuser. Follow the instructions to set it, and you should be ready.

In case you are running on an unsupported architecture, you can open a GitHub issue so that we add its support or use the next steps to build the images locally.

### 

[](https://intuitem.gitbook.io/ciso-assistant/deployment/local#re-building-the-images-locally)

Re-building the images locally

Alternatively, if the previous configuration didn't succeed, run:

### 

[](https://intuitem.gitbook.io/ciso-assistant/deployment/local#ssl-warning)

SSL Warning

Given that Caddy is using a `self-signed certificate`, your browser will mention a warning that you can accept and continue.

[PreviousPrerequisites](https://intuitem.gitbook.io/ciso-assistant/deployment/prerequisites)
[NextDocker rootless configuration](https://intuitem.gitbook.io/ciso-assistant/deployment/docker-rootless-configuration)

Last updated 4 months ago

*   [SSL Warning](https://intuitem.gitbook.io/ciso-assistant/deployment/local#ssl-warning)

Copy

    ./docker-compose-build.sh

# Understanding the IAM model | CISO Assistant

For the complete documentation index, see [llms.txt](https://intuitem.gitbook.io/ciso-assistant/llms.txt)
. This page is also available as [Markdown](https://intuitem.gitbook.io/ciso-assistant/model/organization/understanding-the-iam-model.md)
.

Access security is a foundational aspect of any risk or compliance management platform. In this article, we’ll explore how **authentication**, **authorization**, and **accounting** — the three pillars of the AAA model — are structured and applied within **CISO Assistant**.

* * *

### 

[](https://intuitem.gitbook.io/ciso-assistant/model/organization/understanding-the-iam-model#ember923)

1\. Authentication: SAML vs OIDC

CISO Assistant integrates with leading identity providers (IdPs) via **SAML** and **OIDC**, enabling secure and seamless single sign-on (SSO).

#### 

[](https://intuitem.gitbook.io/ciso-assistant/model/organization/understanding-the-iam-model#ember925)

🔸 SAML

*   legacy protocol based on XML
    
*   common in large enterprises, especially for AD
    
*   browser-based redirection with signed assertions
    

#### 

[](https://intuitem.gitbook.io/ciso-assistant/model/organization/understanding-the-iam-model#ember927)

🔸 OIDC (OpenID Connect)

*   modern standard built on OAuth2
    
*   uses JWT tokens for identity transport
    
*   also browser-based, but more lightweight and versatile
    

> **Recommendation**: If your IdP supports both, **prefer OIDC** — it's more modern, flexible, and aligned with today’s security practices.

* * *

### 

[](https://intuitem.gitbook.io/ciso-assistant/model/organization/understanding-the-iam-model#ember930)

2\. MFA

Multi-Factor Authentication (MFA) is critical for access protection. CISO Assistant supports MFA in two distinct modes, depending on how users authenticate:

#### 

[](https://intuitem.gitbook.io/ciso-assistant/model/organization/understanding-the-iam-model#ember932)

🔸SSO-Based Authentication (SAML / federated OIDC)

*   MFA is handled entirely by the identity provider (IdP)
    
*   the IdP enforces the policy (push notifications, TOTP, biometrics, etc.)
    

#### 

[](https://intuitem.gitbook.io/ciso-assistant/model/organization/understanding-the-iam-model#ember934)

🔸Local Authentication

*   for local accounts, CISO Assistant includes native MFA
    
*   based on **TOTP** (e.g., Google/Microsoft Authenticators)
    

* * *

### 

[](https://intuitem.gitbook.io/ciso-assistant/model/organization/understanding-the-iam-model#ember936)

3\. Authorization: Structured and Hierarchical RBAC

CISO Assistant implements a robust **Role-Based Access Control (RBAC)** model that balances flexibility, clarity, and operational simplicity.

#### 

[](https://intuitem.gitbook.io/ciso-assistant/model/organization/understanding-the-iam-model#ember938)

🔸 Fine-Grained Permissions

Each object type has granular **CRUD permissions** (create, read, update, delete). This model applies across all business entities: users, backups, risks, policies, incidents, data processing, and more. There are more than 200 permissions in CISO Assistant.

#### 

[](https://intuitem.gitbook.io/ciso-assistant/model/organization/understanding-the-iam-model#ember940)

🔸 Predefined Roles

Permissions are grouped into a small set of **standard roles**:

*   **Administrator** – full access to all objects and settings
    
*   **Analyst** – full access to most objects, but cannot modify access control
    
*   **Viewer** – read-only access
    
*   **Approver** – strictly limited to **approving risk acceptance requests**
    

#### 

[](https://intuitem.gitbook.io/ciso-assistant/model/organization/understanding-the-iam-model#ember943)

🔸 Hierarchical Domains

Roles are assigned **within a domain** — a flexible concept representing any relevant business context.

For example, a domain can represent:

*   a **legal entity**
    
*   a **country** or **region**
    
*   a **subsidiary**
    
*   a **business unit**
    
*   any other meaningful organizational structure
    

> Domains are **hierarchical**: a role assigned to a parent domain (e.g., "Group") automatically applies to all its subdomains (e.g., subsidiaries, teams).

#### 

[](https://intuitem.gitbook.io/ciso-assistant/model/organization/understanding-the-iam-model#ember948)

🔸 Role Assignments

Access control is defined via explicit assignments:

> _A role_ ➡️ _on a domain_ ➡️ _for a group of users_

#### 

[](https://intuitem.gitbook.io/ciso-assistant/model/organization/understanding-the-iam-model#ember951)

🔸 User Groups

Users **do not have direct roles**. They inherit permissions through **membership in one or more groups**.

Groups act as the central pivot for managing access:

*   receive role assignments
    
*   grant users permissions via group membership
    
*   defined locally
    
*   optionally synced with an IdP (via external plugin)
    

🚀 This simple yet powerful model accommodates the vast majority of real-world access scenarios. And when needed, the system is fully extensible: it supports **custom roles**, **custom role assignments**, and **custom user groups** to fit even the most specific organizational needs.

* * *

### 

[](https://intuitem.gitbook.io/ciso-assistant/model/organization/understanding-the-iam-model#ember956)

4\. Machine Identity: Personal Access Tokens with Expiration & Control

CISO Assistant doesn’t just secure human access — it also supports secure, auditable access for **automated systems** and **integrations** through **Personal Access Tokens (PATs)**.

#### 

[](https://intuitem.gitbook.io/ciso-assistant/model/organization/understanding-the-iam-model#ember958)

🔸Definition

A **Personal Access Token** is a time-limited secret that allows a script, CI/CD pipeline, or service to authenticate with the platform's API on behalf of a user or machine identity — without requiring an interactive login.

#### 

[](https://intuitem.gitbook.io/ciso-assistant/model/organization/understanding-the-iam-model#ember960)

🔸Key features

*   **time-bounded**: expiration is mandatory
    
*   **RBAC-compliant**: inherits the creator’s permissions
    
*   **revocable**: can be revoked by user or admin
    

#### 

[](https://intuitem.gitbook.io/ciso-assistant/model/organization/understanding-the-iam-model#ember962)

🔸Governance controls

*   admins can restrict who may generate PATs
    
*   all tokens are auditable and managed via UI or API
    

> This ensures **tight control over non-human access**, balancing automation flexibility with strict security hygiene.

### 

[](https://intuitem.gitbook.io/ciso-assistant/model/organization/understanding-the-iam-model#ember969)

5\. Illustration

The following schematic illustrates the fundamental concepts of IAM in CISO Assistant.

![](https://intuitem.gitbook.io/ciso-assistant/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F217025809-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FUJGpmCYDFJNsz2CDasSm%252Fuploads%252F6oosJm53r19PWJ4APZEj%252Frbac.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3Df24afac3-e331-4a5b-b3b6-839b25f8b49f&width=768&dpr=3&quality=100&sign=1199a99a&sv=2)

### 

[](https://intuitem.gitbook.io/ciso-assistant/model/organization/understanding-the-iam-model#id-6.-publication-mechanism)

6\. Publication mechanism

All objects of CISO Assistant support a built-in flag called _**is\_published.**_

Objects with the flag _is\_published_ are visible in subdomains as if they were attached to each subdomain of the object's domain. This mechanism only concerns visibility, not creation/udpate/deletion. All objects are currently published, except assessments (audits, risk analysis, BIA, entitiy assessments)

To avoid an object being published, the simplest solution is to put it in a leaf subdomain.

The plan is to remove this mechanism by Q2 2026 and introduce dynamic groups instead (e.g. the group of all users).

#### 

[](https://intuitem.gitbook.io/ciso-assistant/model/organization/understanding-the-iam-model#can-i-make-an-object-visible-to-all-users-without-attaching-it-to-global)

🤔 Can I make an object visible to all users without attaching it to global?

You can attach this object to a subdomain (e.g. named "published"), and add every user in the group corresponding to reader role on the subdomain. This does not rely on the publication mechanism, and is more generic.

### 

[](https://intuitem.gitbook.io/ciso-assistant/model/organization/understanding-the-iam-model#ember965)

7\. Accounting: Full Audit and Traceability

CISO Assistant includes native tracking of all key actions:

*   logins, restorations, configuration changes, approvals…
    
*   a searchable audit log accessible via the UI or API
    

> This enables complete accountability over critical operations.

### 

[](https://intuitem.gitbook.io/ciso-assistant/model/organization/understanding-the-iam-model#ember969-1)

🧠 In Summary

CISO Assistant's AAA model is built on:

*   **Open standards** (SAML, OIDC, TOTP, RBAC)
    
*   A **structured yet manageable authorization system**
    
*   **secure automation** through scoped, revocable **Personal Access Tokens** (PATs)
    
*   **Built-in traceability** from the ground up
    

It supports complex organizations while remaining readable, scalable, and compliant with modern security expectations.

[PreviousCustom roles](https://intuitem.gitbook.io/ciso-assistant/model/organization/custom-roles)
[NextTeams](https://intuitem.gitbook.io/ciso-assistant/model/organization/teams)

Last updated 4 months ago

# Okta | CISO Assistant

For the complete documentation index, see [llms.txt](https://intuitem.gitbook.io/ciso-assistant/llms.txt)
. This page is also available as [Markdown](https://intuitem.gitbook.io/ciso-assistant/features-focus/sso/identity-providers/okta.md)
.

Go into your **Okta admin console** (it should look like this: `https://<your_url>.okta.com/admin/dashboard`)

1.  In the sidebar menu, click on **Applications > Applications**
    
    ![](https://intuitem.gitbook.io/ciso-assistant/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F217025809-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FUJGpmCYDFJNsz2CDasSm%252Fuploads%252FAYesqWLkeQDiWw640Ij9%252FScreenshot.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3D89f99fe4-a81e-4e73-81c8-c833303ce9bd&width=768&dpr=3&quality=100&sign=24f90ebc&sv=2)
    
2.  Click now on **Create App Integration**
    
    ![](https://intuitem.gitbook.io/ciso-assistant/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F217025809-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FUJGpmCYDFJNsz2CDasSm%252Fuploads%252FdSdR1MRDxoeRULPhYJhj%252FScreenshot%281%29.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3Dc4634784-ed28-4b6a-85ef-4b7464090149&width=768&dpr=3&quality=100&sign=e550153e&sv=2)
    
3.  Select **SAML 2.0** and click on **Next**
    
    ![](https://intuitem.gitbook.io/ciso-assistant/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F217025809-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FUJGpmCYDFJNsz2CDasSm%252Fuploads%252FweUhSro71mwRYB0tbvgy%252FScreenshot%282%29.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3Dbdc5f3c9-bfb7-4b34-8c98-2e94da9520ef&width=768&dpr=3&quality=100&sign=bc75aa5c&sv=2)
    
4.  Choose an **App name** and click on **Next**
    
    ![](https://intuitem.gitbook.io/ciso-assistant/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F217025809-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FUJGpmCYDFJNsz2CDasSm%252Fuploads%252FV7cXJV3E2ptwldQ0LQHK%252FScreenshot%283%29.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3Db7346c58-f0d4-4b47-b69a-290071b0bb01&width=768&dpr=3&quality=100&sign=9d34fe03&sv=2)
    
5.  Add the **Single sign-on** **URL**: `<base_url>/api/accounts/saml/0/acs/` (for example with localhost: `https://localhost:8443/api/accounts/saml/0/acs/`) (see screenshot below)
    
6.  Add the **Audience URI (****SP Entity ID****),** it has to be the same than **SP Entity ID** in CISO Assistant (see screenshot below)
    
7.  Choose **Email** as the **Application username**
    
    ![](https://intuitem.gitbook.io/ciso-assistant/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F217025809-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FUJGpmCYDFJNsz2CDasSm%252Fuploads%252F4Du76vTZapbBlhb75HM5%252FScreenshot%284%29.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3De58e02af-21ab-4f17-a750-25a4cfa6200d&width=768&dpr=3&quality=100&sign=420e0425&sv=2)
    
8.  Add **Attribute Statements**
    
    *   `http://schemas.xmlsoap.org/ws/2005/05/identity/claims/givenname` for user's first name
        
    *   `http://schemas.xmlsoap.org/ws/2005/05/identity/claims/surname` for user's last name
        
    
    ![](https://intuitem.gitbook.io/ciso-assistant/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F217025809-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FUJGpmCYDFJNsz2CDasSm%252Fuploads%252F1MoE2mNEngXH5Uxh7HiL%252FScreenshot%285%29.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3D0a69edde-338c-48e1-b2c6-85ffec659616&width=768&dpr=3&quality=100&sign=524d60e5&sv=2)
    
9.  Click on **Next** and fill in the **Feedback** page as you wish then click on **Finish**
    
    ![](https://intuitem.gitbook.io/ciso-assistant/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F217025809-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FUJGpmCYDFJNsz2CDasSm%252Fuploads%252FwAxCOWH5I62vwYUuYccR%252FScreenshot%286%29.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3Df045c8a4-af09-4e74-a50e-084017825488&width=768&dpr=3&quality=100&sign=69a8e40c&sv=2)
    
    ![](https://intuitem.gitbook.io/ciso-assistant/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F217025809-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FUJGpmCYDFJNsz2CDasSm%252Fuploads%252FfyEIIB8gv7l4plELSWYm%252FScreenshot%287%29.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3D48c83acf-5ca6-44e7-a448-957440b99354&width=768&dpr=3&quality=100&sign=60fbbadc&sv=2)
    
10.  In the **Settings** box inside **SAML 2.0:**
    
    *   Copy the **Metadata URL** and paste it into the **Metadata URL** field in CISO Assistant
        
    *   Copy the **Issuer** url and paste it into the **IdP Entity ID** field in CISO Assistant
        
    
    ![](https://intuitem.gitbook.io/ciso-assistant/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F217025809-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FUJGpmCYDFJNsz2CDasSm%252Fuploads%252FawwU2wsQIx4AvIDxbew1%252FScreenshot%288%29.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3Da04a085a-32b1-484a-8c37-384c2438c8c1&width=768&dpr=3&quality=100&sign=210606cc&sv=2)
    
11.  Go to the **Assignments** tab
    
    ![](https://intuitem.gitbook.io/ciso-assistant/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F217025809-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FUJGpmCYDFJNsz2CDasSm%252Fuploads%252FhrgmtuD2JoleiXxjPHbM%252FScreenshot%289%29.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3Dc9cf59b1-6e31-490b-b30f-e6670dce8a66&width=768&dpr=3&quality=100&sign=ea3af4fb&sv=2)
    
12.  Click on **Assign** and choose whether you want to assign users or specific groups
    
    ![](https://intuitem.gitbook.io/ciso-assistant/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F217025809-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FUJGpmCYDFJNsz2CDasSm%252Fuploads%252F3MIUKjgpmo09QPMv0tu8%252FScreenshot%2810%29.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3D760643ee-56e0-4a86-a07b-c2e425bfea27&width=768&dpr=3&quality=100&sign=d19e5909&sv=2)
    

Add a user in your application doesn't automatically create the user on CISO Assistant

You can now [configure CISO Assistant](https://intuitem.gitbook.io/ciso-assistant/features-highlights/sso#configure-ciso-assistant-with-saml)
 with the **3 parameters** you've retrieved.

[PreviousMicrosoft Entra ID](https://intuitem.gitbook.io/ciso-assistant/features-focus/sso/identity-providers/microsoft-entra-id)
[NextGoogle Workspace](https://intuitem.gitbook.io/ciso-assistant/features-focus/sso/identity-providers/google-workplace)

# Upgrading a library | CISO Assistant

For the complete documentation index, see [llms.txt](https://intuitem.gitbook.io/ciso-assistant/llms.txt)
. This page is also available as [Markdown](https://intuitem.gitbook.io/ciso-assistant/deployment/upgrading-a-library.md)
.

In you've updated your instance and didn't see the changes on a loaded library, you can do the following to refresh the library to the latest version:

![](https://intuitem.gitbook.io/ciso-assistant/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F217025809-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FUJGpmCYDFJNsz2CDasSm%252Fuploads%252F7nASXn8PcfRbFEBBGWz9%252Fscsh-2025-01-01-10.09.59.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3Da8c50bfe-f4d8-45d2-b5ea-aeddf12a12ef&width=768&dpr=3&quality=100&sign=c61157ca&sv=2)

This also applies to custom framework as long as you respect the incremental step of the library's version.

# Manage extended result | CISO Assistant

For the complete documentation index, see [llms.txt](https://intuitem.gitbook.io/ciso-assistant/llms.txt)
. This page is also available as [Markdown](https://intuitem.gitbook.io/ciso-assistant/model/compliance/manage-extended-result.md)
.

[](https://intuitem.gitbook.io/ciso-assistant/model/compliance/manage-extended-result#manage-minor-nonconformities-and-audit-results-efficiently)

[Manage Minor Nonconformities And Audit Results Efficiently](https://app.guidde.com/playbooks/tfJoxjgR2GViiWgprnp1hn)



-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

This tutorial guides you through managing minor nonconformities and major audit results within your compliance assessments

#### 

[](https://intuitem.gitbook.io/ciso-assistant/model/compliance/manage-extended-result#go-to-your-instance)

Go to your instance

#### 

[](https://intuitem.gitbook.io/ciso-assistant/model/compliance/manage-extended-result#id-1.-introduction)

1\. Introduction

You will learn how to add extra attribute to your audit through extended result.

![](https://intuitem.gitbook.io/ciso-assistant/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2Fstatic.guidde.com%2Fv0%2Fqg%252FJ0RVKao966SmT5uQXRHVpcgc2yd2%252FtfJoxjgR2GViiWgprnp1hn%252FafRc7XrhcmCnoYZph2xWjV_doc.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3D30d72ef0-ff8a-4bee-b019-f3d871b40219&width=768&dpr=3&quality=100&sign=f8b35e0a&sv=2)

Introduction

#### 

[](https://intuitem.gitbook.io/ciso-assistant/model/compliance/manage-extended-result#id-2.-open-your-audit)

2\. Open your audit

Click "ISO 27002 SOA" to access the relevant compliance assessment for managing audit results.

![](https://intuitem.gitbook.io/ciso-assistant/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2Fstatic.guidde.com%2Fv0%2Fqg%252FJ0RVKao966SmT5uQXRHVpcgc2yd2%252FtfJoxjgR2GViiWgprnp1hn%252Fj1VL7jnL2eroQcG62W5oeb_doc.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3D768fc383-898b-42b9-bf4d-658ea1384470&width=768&dpr=3&quality=100&sign=cf356367&sv=2)

Open ISO 27002 SOA Assessment

#### 

[](https://intuitem.gitbook.io/ciso-assistant/model/compliance/manage-extended-result#id-3.-enter-edit-mode)

3\. Enter Edit Mode

Click "Edit" to enable modifications on the selected compliance assessment.

![](https://intuitem.gitbook.io/ciso-assistant/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2Fstatic.guidde.com%2Fv0%2Fqg%252FJ0RVKao966SmT5uQXRHVpcgc2yd2%252FtfJoxjgR2GViiWgprnp1hn%252Forw9CaCJAXvg8kdRM7HCoy_doc.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3Da181a480-c9e7-46ec-8530-09e68173271e&width=768&dpr=3&quality=100&sign=cda1ee32&sv=2)

Enter Edit Mode

#### 

[](https://intuitem.gitbook.io/ciso-assistant/model/compliance/manage-extended-result#id-4.-access-more-options)

4\. Access More Options

Click "More" to reveal additional settings and options for the assessment.

![](https://intuitem.gitbook.io/ciso-assistant/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2Fstatic.guidde.com%2Fv0%2Fqg%252FJ0RVKao966SmT5uQXRHVpcgc2yd2%252FtfJoxjgR2GViiWgprnp1hn%252F5a4xNe5eu82T16YFp4YWaP_doc.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3D40bbd64c-ec76-48af-8204-af6735aa04b3&width=768&dpr=3&quality=100&sign=95dcdc0b&sv=2)

Access More Options

#### 

[](https://intuitem.gitbook.io/ciso-assistant/model/compliance/manage-extended-result#id-5.-enable-extended-result)

5\. Enable extended result

Click "on" to activate the desired feature or option within the assessment settings.

![](https://intuitem.gitbook.io/ciso-assistant/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2Fstatic.guidde.com%2Fv0%2Fqg%252FJ0RVKao966SmT5uQXRHVpcgc2yd2%252FtfJoxjgR2GViiWgprnp1hn%252FvZsoTYBQguqAo61YCTCQdz_doc.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3Dce8b91b0-6e23-4bcf-8b87-68077cdd55a1&width=768&dpr=3&quality=100&sign=264d65d9&sv=2)

Enable Specific Setting

#### 

[](https://intuitem.gitbook.io/ciso-assistant/model/compliance/manage-extended-result#id-7.-save-audit-changes)

7\. Save audit Changes

Click "Save" to apply and store the changes made to the compliance assessment.

![](https://intuitem.gitbook.io/ciso-assistant/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2Fstatic.guidde.com%2Fv0%2Fqg%252FJ0RVKao966SmT5uQXRHVpcgc2yd2%252FtfJoxjgR2GViiWgprnp1hn%252FtiKYvUWatYdcAd9KZGcbRH_doc.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3D23b8061a-9ff8-40ee-ad5f-71096b8289f0&width=768&dpr=3&quality=100&sign=92328bef&sv=2)

Save Assessment Changes

#### 

[](https://intuitem.gitbook.io/ciso-assistant/model/compliance/manage-extended-result#id-10.-open-a-requirement)

10\. Open a requirement

Click "4.1 - Understanding the organization and its context" to examine specific requirements.

![](https://intuitem.gitbook.io/ciso-assistant/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2Fstatic.guidde.com%2Fv0%2Fqg%252FJ0RVKao966SmT5uQXRHVpcgc2yd2%252FtfJoxjgR2GViiWgprnp1hn%252FvkbffqqNuYVzRYAFxjpsJ4_doc.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3D32cf95d4-024d-48f8-a0d9-1dd3cd7ca791&width=768&dpr=3&quality=100&sign=e77076b5&sv=2)

Open Context Subsection

#### 

[](https://intuitem.gitbook.io/ciso-assistant/model/compliance/manage-extended-result#id-11.-choose-the-value-for-your-extended-result)

11\. Choose the value for your extended result

Select the appropriate category such as major nonconformity, minor nonconformity, observation, opportunity for improvement, or good practice.

![](https://intuitem.gitbook.io/ciso-assistant/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2Fstatic.guidde.com%2Fv0%2Fqg%252FJ0RVKao966SmT5uQXRHVpcgc2yd2%252FtfJoxjgR2GViiWgprnp1hn%252FmDK4VZ1rkF2zup9uCNGw2q_doc.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3D4f817784-90b7-4fb7-86fe-26e60e7d4eb2&width=768&dpr=3&quality=100&sign=d4413ea2&sv=2)

Choose Nonconformity Type

#### 

[](https://intuitem.gitbook.io/ciso-assistant/model/compliance/manage-extended-result#id-14.-make-sure-its-consistent-with-the-audit-result)

14\. Make sure it's consistent with the audit result

Click the note stating "Major and minor nonconformities are only applicable when result is non-compliant or partially compliant." to understand criteria.

![](https://intuitem.gitbook.io/ciso-assistant/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2Fstatic.guidde.com%2Fv0%2Fqg%252FJ0RVKao966SmT5uQXRHVpcgc2yd2%252FtfJoxjgR2GViiWgprnp1hn%252FnF9EAnNMomWES5R8ASqweo_doc.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3De1ae0a1b-bb4e-45ed-b13b-3ca9c8a07388&width=768&dpr=3&quality=100&sign=c4f4dbcf&sv=2)

Review Nonconformity Applicability

#### 

[](https://intuitem.gitbook.io/ciso-assistant/model/compliance/manage-extended-result#id-17.-select-the-value-and-save)

17\. Select the value and save

Click "Save" to store the additional nonconformity or observation details.

![](https://intuitem.gitbook.io/ciso-assistant/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2Fstatic.guidde.com%2Fv0%2Fqg%252FJ0RVKao966SmT5uQXRHVpcgc2yd2%252FtfJoxjgR2GViiWgprnp1hn%252FxeGyNXVcfNnyPqEToY8KVe_doc.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3D37965077-966d-463b-98e7-b34c4e8306df&width=768&dpr=3&quality=100&sign=61df6b3a&sv=2)

Save Additional Entry

#### 

[](https://intuitem.gitbook.io/ciso-assistant/model/compliance/manage-extended-result#id-21.-use-the-observation-field-for-more-information)

21\. Use the Observation field for more Information

Click "Save" to finalize and save the observation or nonconformity information entered.

![](https://intuitem.gitbook.io/ciso-assistant/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2Fstatic.guidde.com%2Fv0%2Fqg%252FJ0RVKao966SmT5uQXRHVpcgc2yd2%252FtfJoxjgR2GViiWgprnp1hn%252FbdL8REWuvPb26ZorthrWfH_doc.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3D540844c2-f9ea-4b23-99ad-7827169aa45e&width=768&dpr=3&quality=100&sign=894ae1dc&sv=2)

Save Observation Information

You have successfully managed minor nonconformities and major audit results by editing, documenting, and saving relevant compliance assessment details. This ensures accurate tracking and supports effective audit management for your organization.

[PreviousCompliance](https://intuitem.gitbook.io/ciso-assistant/model/compliance)
[NextDomain export/import](https://intuitem.gitbook.io/ciso-assistant/model/domain-export-import)

SELINUX

If you have selinux enabled on your distro, you might want to check if it's not preventing the mount volume of the docker compose; you can try something like this:

Copy

    chcon -Rt svirt_sandbox_file_t ./db

# Custom certificates | CISO Assistant

For the complete documentation index, see [llms.txt](https://intuitem.gitbook.io/ciso-assistant/llms.txt)
. This page is also available as [Markdown](https://intuitem.gitbook.io/ciso-assistant/deployment/custom-certificates.md)
.

You can configure your own Certificate by replacing the line `tls internal` in the docker-compose.yml by `tls <cert_file> <key_file>`. Here is Caddy documentation on this [https://caddyserver.com/docs/caddyfile/directives/tls](https://caddyserver.com/docs/caddyfile/directives/tls)

Before doing this, there is just one step, you need to add the `cert_file` and the `key_file` inside caddy container.

You have basically two ways to do it:

*   Adding the two files inside `caddy_data` directory, as it is already mounted by default in the volumes, and specify the path to the files:
    

Copy

    caddy:
        container_name: caddy
        image: caddy:2.10.0
        ...
        volumes:
          - ./caddy_data:/data
        command: |
          sh -c 'echo $$CISO_ASSISTANT_URL "{
          reverse_proxy /api/* backend:8000
          reverse_proxy /* frontend:3000
          tls /data/<path>/cert_file /data/<path>/key_file
          }" > Caddyfile && caddy run'

*   If you don’t have this volume or you want to add another, create a repository at the same level of your docker compose file for example `/certs`, add the files inside and moun it:
    

Copy

    caddy:
        container_name: caddy
        image: caddy:2.10.0
        ...
        volumes:
          - ./caddy_data:/data
          - ./certs:/certs
        command: |
          sh -c 'echo $$CISO_ASSISTANT_URL "{
          reverse_proxy /api/* backend:8000
          reverse_proxy /* frontend:3000
          tls /certs/cert_file /certs/key_file
          }" > Caddyfile && caddy run'

[PreviousDeploy on a VPS](https://intuitem.gitbook.io/ciso-assistant/deployment/deploy-on-a-vps)
[NextManaging Secrets](https://intuitem.gitbook.io/ciso-assistant/deployment/managing-secrets)

Last updated 6 months ago

Was this helpful?

Was this helpful?

# Docker rootless configuration | CISO Assistant

For the complete documentation index, see [llms.txt](https://intuitem.gitbook.io/ciso-assistant/llms.txt)
. This page is also available as [Markdown](https://intuitem.gitbook.io/ciso-assistant/deployment/docker-rootless-configuration.md)
.

> Since V3.16, CISO Assistant now runs as non-root user 1001:1001 by default across all compose templates.

If you already have a local instance of CISO Assistant, please refer to the migration guide

[](https://intuitem.gitbook.io/ciso-assistant/deployment/docker-rootless-configuration#fresh-install)

Fresh install


------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

If you are new from Ciso-Assistant, you will automatically be deployed with a rootless Docker configuration by running pre-built images or local image build

### 

[](https://intuitem.gitbook.io/ciso-assistant/deployment/docker-rootless-configuration#using-pre-built-images)

Using pre-built images

Copy

    ./docker-compose.sh

### 

[](https://intuitem.gitbook.io/ciso-assistant/deployment/docker-rootless-configuration#using-image-local-build)

Using image local build

Copy

    ./docker-compose-build.sh

[](https://intuitem.gitbook.io/ciso-assistant/deployment/docker-rootless-configuration#migration-guide)

Migration guide


----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

You already have a self-hosted Ciso Assistant (Community version or On-Premise Pro version) and you want to know all the options you have:

I want a rootless Docker and I am currently running CISO Assistant with pre-built images[](https://intuitem.gitbook.io/ciso-assistant/deployment/docker-rootless-configuration#i-want-a-rootless-docker-and-i-am-currently-running-ciso-assistant-with-pre-built-images)

#### 

[](https://intuitem.gitbook.io/ciso-assistant/deployment/docker-rootless-configuration#you-are-using-docker-compose.yml-to-deploy-ciso-assistant)

You are using docker-compose.yml to deploy Ciso Assistant

Copy

    git pull
    docker compose down
    sudo chown -R 1001:1001 ./db

Then update your docker-compose.yml on the version you want (ex: v3.16) or keep latest tag and then ignore the manual update in your file.

Copy

    docker compose up -d

Your new containers should be root-less!

#### 

[](https://intuitem.gitbook.io/ciso-assistant/deployment/docker-rootless-configuration#you-are-using-a-custom-.yml-to-deploy-ciso-assistant)

You are using a custom .yml to deploy Ciso Assistant

If you have any doubt about updating your custom .yml, do not hesitate to contact us on our Discord or Support portal.

I want a rootless Docker and I am currently running CISO Assistant with local images[](https://intuitem.gitbook.io/ciso-assistant/deployment/docker-rootless-configuration#i-want-a-rootless-docker-and-i-am-currently-running-ciso-assistant-with-local-images)

Copy

    git pull
    docker compose down
    sudo chown -R 1001:1001 ./db
    docker compose -f docker-compose-build.yml up -d 

[](https://intuitem.gitbook.io/ciso-assistant/deployment/docker-rootless-configuration#keep-root-docker)

Keep root Docker


------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

In the case you do not want to have rootless Docker

Keep the root Docker as it was before[](https://intuitem.gitbook.io/ciso-assistant/deployment/docker-rootless-configuration#keep-the-root-docker-as-it-was-before)

Then manually update your docker-compose.yml on the images version you want (ex: v3.16). Ignore this step if you use latest image

That is it! Since you did not update the github repository, the docker-compose.yml keeps the initial form without root less Docker configuration

In the case you did update the github repository by doing a _git pull_ command, we suggest you to take an older version of the file (like the v3.15.5 docker-compose.yml version)

[](https://intuitem.gitbook.io/ciso-assistant/deployment/docker-rootless-configuration#simple-rootless-check)

Simple rootless check


----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

If you want to verify if you run a rootless Docker container, do:

It should say :

[PreviousLocal](https://intuitem.gitbook.io/ciso-assistant/deployment/local)
[NextRemote/Virtualization](https://intuitem.gitbook.io/ciso-assistant/deployment/remote-virtualization)

Last updated 2 months ago

Was this helpful?

*   [Fresh install](https://intuitem.gitbook.io/ciso-assistant/deployment/docker-rootless-configuration#fresh-install)
    
*   [Using pre-built images](https://intuitem.gitbook.io/ciso-assistant/deployment/docker-rootless-configuration#using-pre-built-images)
    
*   [Using image local build](https://intuitem.gitbook.io/ciso-assistant/deployment/docker-rootless-configuration#using-image-local-build)
    
*   [Migration guide](https://intuitem.gitbook.io/ciso-assistant/deployment/docker-rootless-configuration#migration-guide)
    
*   [Keep root Docker](https://intuitem.gitbook.io/ciso-assistant/deployment/docker-rootless-configuration#keep-root-docker)
    
*   [Simple rootless check](https://intuitem.gitbook.io/ciso-assistant/deployment/docker-rootless-configuration#simple-rootless-check)
    

Was this helpful?

Copy

    docker compose down

Copy

    image: ghcr.io/intuitem/ciso-assistant-community/frontend:v3.15.2
    # replace with (for example)
    image: ghcr.io/intuitem/ciso-assistant-community/frontend:v3.16

Copy

    docker compose up -d

Copy

    docker exec -it backend id  

Copy

    uid=1001 gid=1001 groups=1001

# Updating your local instance | CISO Assistant

For the complete documentation index, see [llms.txt](https://intuitem.gitbook.io/ciso-assistant/llms.txt)
. This page is also available as [Markdown](https://intuitem.gitbook.io/ciso-assistant/deployment/updating-your-local-instance.md)
.

[](https://intuitem.gitbook.io/ciso-assistant/deployment/updating-your-local-instance#hands-free)

Hands-free


-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

The easiest way to update your on-prem/local instance (pro or community)

**Run the script** _**update-ciso-assistant**_**:**

Copy

    ./update-ciso-assistant.sh

[](https://intuitem.gitbook.io/ciso-assistant/deployment/updating-your-local-instance#detailled-steps)

Detailled steps


---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

In case of issues (unsupported shell, windows, etc.) here are the steps to consider:

1.  backup your db:
    
    1.  if you're using `sqlite`, copy the file under a different name
        
    2.  if it's `postgresql` you can use something like `pgdump`
        
    

1.  stop and clean the containers, this won't affect your data
    

`docker compose rm -fs`

1.  restart the compose and let it handle the migration
    

`docker compose up -d`

[](https://intuitem.gitbook.io/ciso-assistant/deployment/updating-your-local-instance#edge-cases)

Edge cases


-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

**Force remove the previous docker images to get the new ones**

[PreviousSetting up mailer](https://intuitem.gitbook.io/ciso-assistant/deployment/setting-up-mailer)
[NextHelm Chart](https://intuitem.gitbook.io/ciso-assistant/deployment/helm-chart)

Last updated 6 months ago

Was this helpful?

*   [Hands-free](https://intuitem.gitbook.io/ciso-assistant/deployment/updating-your-local-instance#hands-free)
    
*   [Detailled steps](https://intuitem.gitbook.io/ciso-assistant/deployment/updating-your-local-instance#detailled-steps)
    
*   [Edge cases](https://intuitem.gitbook.io/ciso-assistant/deployment/updating-your-local-instance#edge-cases)
    

Was this helpful?

Copy

    docker rmi ghcr.io/intuitem/ciso-assistant-community/backend:latest ghcr.io/intuitem/ciso-assistant-community/frontend:latest 2> /dev/null

# Custom roles | CISO Assistant

For the complete documentation index, see [llms.txt](https://intuitem.gitbook.io/ciso-assistant/llms.txt)
. This page is also available as [Markdown](https://intuitem.gitbook.io/ciso-assistant/model/organization/custom-roles.md)
.

**Notice:** Custom roles allow you to refine access control when very specific permissions need to be granted to a user.

In CISO Assistant, **domains are the primary mechanism for restricting access**. Custom roles should only be created when domain-based restrictions are insufficient.

Keep in mind that custom roles increase IAM complexity and make access reviews more difficult. In most cases, the default roles are sufficient.

[](https://intuitem.gitbook.io/ciso-assistant/model/organization/custom-roles#custom-roles-for-ciso-assistant)

[Custom roles for CISO Assistant](https://app.guidde.com/playbooks/7f23K23PveNou6UuXdYRFe)



---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Learn how to create and customize roles such as DPO and OPS within your organization

#### 

[](https://intuitem.gitbook.io/ciso-assistant/model/organization/custom-roles#sign-in-as-an-admin-on-your-ciso-assistant-instance-and-follow-the-steps-below)

Sign in as an Admin on your CISO Assistant instance and follow the steps below.

#### 

[](https://intuitem.gitbook.io/ciso-assistant/model/organization/custom-roles#id-1.-introduction)

1\. Introduction

This guide walks you through setting permissions and assigning user groups to streamline your CISO Assistant's role management.

# Helm Chart | CISO Assistant

For the complete documentation index, see [llms.txt](https://intuitem.gitbook.io/ciso-assistant/llms.txt)
. This page is also available as [Markdown](https://intuitem.gitbook.io/ciso-assistant/deployment/helm-chart.md)
.

### 

[](https://intuitem.gitbook.io/ciso-assistant/deployment/helm-chart#gh-oci-registry)

GH OCI registry

1.  Getting the values
    

Copy

    helm show values oci://ghcr.io/intuitem/helm-charts/ce/ciso-assistant > custom.yaml

1.  customize as you see fit
    
2.  Install the chart
    

Copy

    helm install ciso-assistant-release oci://ghcr.io/intuitem/helm-charts/ce/ciso-assistant -f custom.yaml

### 

[](https://intuitem.gitbook.io/ciso-assistant/deployment/helm-chart#legacy)

Legacy

> **Note:** The old Helm repository (`intuitem.github.io/ca-helm-chart`) is no longer maintained. Please use the OCI registry above for new installations.

# Setting up S3 | CISO Assistant

For the complete documentation index, see [llms.txt](https://intuitem.gitbook.io/ciso-assistant/llms.txt)
. This page is also available as [Markdown](https://intuitem.gitbook.io/ciso-assistant/deployment/setting-up-s3.md)
.

By default, CISO Assistant stores attachments on the local filesystem. You can configure it to use an S3-compatible object storage (AWS S3, MinIO, etc.).

### 

[](https://intuitem.gitbook.io/ciso-assistant/deployment/setting-up-s3#prerequisitories)

Prerequisitories

*   A running S3-compatible storage
    
*   An existing bucket (must be created **before** starting CISO Assistant)
    
*   Valid access credentials (Access Key / Secret Key)
    

### 

[](https://intuitem.gitbook.io/ciso-assistant/deployment/setting-up-s3#configure-environment-variables)

Configure environment variables

Set the following environment variables in the backend environment:

Copy

    export USE_S3=True
    export AWS_ACCESS_KEY_ID=<your-access-key>
    export AWS_SECRET_ACCESS_KEY=<your-secret-key>
    export AWS_STORAGE_BUCKET_NAME=<your-bucket-name>
    export AWS_S3_ENDPOINT_URL=<your-s3-endpoint>

That's it ! You can now launch your backend and your attachments will be sent to your S3 🔥

### 

[](https://intuitem.gitbook.io/ciso-assistant/deployment/setting-up-s3#example-case-local-minio-block-storage)

Example case : local MinIO block storage

You can test S3 support using MinIO:

Copy

    docker run -d \
      --name minio \
      -p 9000:9000 \
      -p 9001:9001 \
      -e MINIO_ROOT_USER=ciso-assistant-admin \
      -e MINIO_ROOT_PASSWORD=not_secure_password \
      -v minio_data:/data \
      minio/minio server /data --console-address ":9001"

Then go on [http://localhost:9001](http://localhost:9001/)
 , enter your minio root user/password and create a bucket with the name 'my-ciso-bucket'.

The backend environment variables will be:

You can now see your attachments on the MinIO console after importing them in ciso-assistant.

[PreviousFrequent questions](https://intuitem.gitbook.io/ciso-assistant/deployment/frequent-questions)
[NextSetting up mailer](https://intuitem.gitbook.io/ciso-assistant/deployment/setting-up-mailer)

Last updated 6 months ago

Was this helpful?

*   [Prerequisitories](https://intuitem.gitbook.io/ciso-assistant/deployment/setting-up-s3#prerequisitories)
    
*   [Configure environment variables](https://intuitem.gitbook.io/ciso-assistant/deployment/setting-up-s3#configure-environment-variables)
    
*   [Example case : local MinIO block storage](https://intuitem.gitbook.io/ciso-assistant/deployment/setting-up-s3#example-case-local-minio-block-storage)
    

Was this helpful?

Copy

    export USE_S3=True
    export AWS_ACCESS_KEY_ID=ciso-assistant-admin
    export AWS_SECRET_ACCESS_KEY=not_secure_password
    export AWS_STORAGE_BUCKET_NAME=my-ciso-bucket
    export AWS_S3_ENDPOINT_URL=http://localhost:9000
